Since they hadn't broken up, they can have him occasionally talk to her on the phone without showing her or even speaking like just on the phone sort of conversation without seeing the other person. This is one of the ways i thought could really drive home the Sam-struggling part of the story as it really makes him feel alone as well, with Wheelie and Brains just being there for some slight emotional support but not really filling that empty void of wanting to be something more, as the movie wanted to portray him as. they could even have him wanting to propose but still be hesitant since he knows that with his current bad luck, he might not be ready for it and it could be a whole thing of building up that confidence again as the story goes, which is something i'll mention later. as for other motivations regarding how they can patch over it, they could've just made Dylan like some sort of fan who kinda knows him and who builds a connection with Sam who thinks that he mightve found his lucky break, still gives enough reason to give him that job recommendation at Accuretta. this fits the next part of the story where Carly gets kidnapped and Dylan reveals his alliance with the decepticons, where Sam thought that he found a friend in Dylan but then that big reveal happens and honestly make the same threat with his parents or even Mikaela as he knows about her using the same watch decepticon and shit. As for why he even wanted to go to Chicago in the first place, it didnt have to just be because he wanted to save his girl. this would be an amazing opportunity for Sam to showcase what he wanted to be as: as someone who can be a hero for the world. We could have him be unreasonably motivated to go confront Dylan and try to stop the Decepticons from taking over the world because of what they did to his friends, the Autobots, and to finally prove that he can be someone special. Now as the rest of that amazing 2nd half happens, after saving the day, he finally builds that confidence of knowing that he can be someone special inside and makes that final call to Mikaela wanting to go see her, with Bumblebee giving the rings as the conversation goes.  i know this part is probably ignorable at best since it just doesnt seem like they would've even tried to rewrite the entire script and that Michael Bay really just wanted that dumb love interest story element. heck, im basically saying all of this because i truly believe that storyline with Carly did not need to exist. this suggestion i made, imo, should give Sam a more personal motivation rather than a generic love interest of sorts and helps builds him up as the hero he can be and who he wants to be on his own accord, which can really settle his arc for good. As for Mikaela, she didnt need an arc at all. she can really just be offscreen for all we care and still have some sort of emotional weight on Sam as he struggles to find purpose. I genuinely think they couldve written a better story for Sam without Carly's presence but I guess thats just my opinion..

I'll never forget when I moved to Chicago for college in 2010. I was so excited to be studying film in a big city, and this was right after The Dark Knight had come out, so of course I was going nuts seeing all those locations right around me. One day early into that first year, a bunch of us who all lived in the  same dorm hall went out for pizza together, and saw that a professional film crew was shooting something in an alley nearby. They had a GIANT light suspended from a crane, I'd never seen anything like it before. I was so thrilled, and I wondered... could it be the next Batman movie? I approached some of the people standing nearby and asked if they knew what movie it was.  They said, "I think it's a new Transformers movie."  "...oh.", I said.  Then I went back to eating my pizza.  I still haven't seen this movie. Everything I know about it comes from YouTube videos.

Maybe I'm talking nonsense, but I've never seen Optimus killing Sentinel or Megatron as "out of character", or rather...out of character. Sentinel has proven to be a traitor and to have always been Megatron's ally, while the latter has already resurrected twice (the first time in the 2007 film, after centuries of inactivity and essentially left for dead by the Autobots and Decepticons, the second time in Revenge of the Fallen), and has proven to be a terrible thorn in the side.   Why would Optimus spare someone who made deception one of his main weapons?  Let's remember how Megatron has always taken advantage of Optimus' distraction to strike him from behind, or taking advantage of a momentary numerical advantage.   In short, as far as Optimus is concerned in these films (at least until the third), he's good, yes, but not an idiot.

I don't know if I've seen anyone point this out, but Dark of The Moon is just a slightly modified version of the G1 series of episodes "Megatron's Master Plan" combined with "The Ultimate Doom".  Megatron turns humans against the Autobots.  That's lifted from Megatron's Master Plan.  Cybertron is brought into Earth's orbit.  That's from The Ultimate Doom.  Autobots are forced to leave on a human ship.  Megatron's Master Plan AGAIN.  Decepticons enslaving humanity is from those episodes too.  Decepticons working with humans is from those episodes.  Megatron taking the Lincoln Memorial and sitting on it as a throne is just lifted directly from G1.  It's either the Master Plan episodes again, or "Atlantis, Arise!"  Either way, it's still just the 80s again.  The first three movies are just G1 plot lines but made more edgy.  Sun harvester?  "Changing Gears".  World travel?  Season 2 is full of it.  Carly as a character was lifted from G1, though she has zero resemblance to the 80s character besides being blonde and the love interest of the main human character.  There's probably more that I'm forgetting too.

Tone is what works well in a movie or in a book. When Optimus slowly becomes a killing machine, the tone doesnâ€™t feel how it should feel. It ignores the â€œOptimus is crazyâ€ for a hero feeling. The best comparison for this is the Image comics run on the Transformers.   In the Image comics, the war and the destruction from these giant metal robots destroying both buildings and people is a heavy saddening feeling. Optimus and his autobots have no issue taking aim at the cons and killing them but each death takes a piece of the character with them. The whole atmosphere of the comic is â€œthis is their reality, in reality people die, this is what would happenâ€. Thatâ€™s probably the biggest difference between this movie and other transformers media. When a city is destroyed or even a species due to the fighting, it weighs heavy on a character as it should but in the bayverse people donâ€™t really care, itâ€™s just another day for them. Itâ€™s weird how the tone is so off.

Thus Megatron would retrieve the Allspark and by the time Sentinel and the other Decepticons were able to arrive on Earth, they would activate the pillars, bringing Cybertron to Earth's Orbit and then they would've used the allspark to return all live on Cybertron   But it all failed when Megatron crash-landed on the Earth, while Sentinel crash-landed on the moon. God, I hated this movie. The way it so dramatically shifted from the tone of the first two. Its almost as drastic as the tonal shift between the first two Hyperdimension Neptunia games. The first two movies were somewhat serious, but pretty goofy big bot battle beat-offs and we loved them for it. The second film, I didnt mind the more serious tone, what with building on the lore of ancient Cybertron and the  Fallen. It helped with worldbuilding Cybertron as a place with its own history and culture. The third film IMMEDIATELY jumps down your fucking throat with conspiracy, human corruption and collaboration and outright fucking WAR CRIMES. Sure, a movie where the good guys gets trounced by a much stronger force and have to build a resistance from the back foot is a good plot device, but it was handled so poorly here. In addition, like the much darker tone implies, this film took itself WAY too seriously. This is Transformers for fuck's sake, not a CoD story. Lastly, Id actually heard Bayverse 'formers was supposed to end here, with Megatron realising this back and forth brawling was going fucking nowhere for their race, and forming a truce with Optimus to get Cybertron back on its feet. Lastly, this movie can genuinely go fuck itself for killing off Ironhide. When a story kills off a major plot/series important character like this, it REEKS of a shit attempt to raise the stakes. Jazz dying in Transformers 1 was good IMO, because it depicted Megatron as this absolutely evil, near-invincible, horrifyingly strong titan of a Decepticon, and that ANYTHING fucking around with him was gonna find out. Messily. Ironhide dying in such a mediocre way (IN ONE SHOT NO LESS. I dont care if Sentinel is a Prime, that kind of power should NOT be written off as some kind of on-hand weapon thats never used again) was downright insulting to his character and his fans.

"THE HONOR IS MINE" Why? Sure, for we humans, what Buzz and his team managed was the most impressive feat we've managed thus far, but in the greater scheme of the cosmos, it's the first little step out of many steps to come. The Cybertronians are robots that can turn into space vehicles if they want, to them what Buzz achieved would be virtually nothing. Imagine having to act like a literal baby taking its first step is the most impressive damn thing you ever saw, and that witnessing it is a massive honor to you. How could anyone rip on Optimus' changing personality throughout the films??? This is a franchise spanning decades.  Sure, Bayverse is a whole new continuity but it still follows the backgound lore. The violence in this is pretty damn justified, as well as Optimus' pretty drastic personality change. By this point, the Autobots and Decepticons have been fighting each other for MILLIONS of years, to the point where their planet is a barren wasteland and they're ALL living on borrowed time because natural Energon no longer exists, it needs to be created.  Optimus, this dude has been on the losing side the whole duration of the war, watching his friends die and simply knowing Shockwave exists (dude is messed up). And then he's got his nemesis, Megatron.  You've been fighting this dude for millions of years. You've killed each other COUNTLESS times and you both keep coming back for more. Megatron is a gladiator, a warlord and has no attachments to anyone but himself and his love for his home Planet. He loves the fact he can't really get rid of Optimus and Optimus can't get rid of him, even though he completely despises him. Meanwhile Optimus has tried every diplomatic solution and is beyond done with the Decepticons and Megatron's shit, he's fighting for peace and for freedom of ALL life in the universe. He just can't seem to put this dude down for good and peace is something Megatron will never want unless it's all under his control.  His friends now number in the single digits. And finally, Optimus finds a new ally and an old friend with Sentinel, something that has a very very slim chance of happening to him considering all of the above... Only to be betrayed by that friend, his very own Mentor.  So yeah, I imagine you'd be willing to tear a few faces and heads off considering all these facts. War Crime Prime is best prime because, put simply, he's got the most Human reaction of all the Transformers. And ALL of it is completely justified. Even then, it took MILLIONS of years for him to finally snap. That's some godly self-control when you take everything I've said into consideration.   Cut War Crime Prime some slack. Dude was always trying his best and it was never enough over millions of years and even dying countless times. Naturally, all of this will force him to realize, that to protect life, sometimes you have to take it away.   Thanks for coming to my Ted talk.

Somehow, the fuel rods returned...
So, Megatron's plan. The way I always saw it, the civil war happened over the period of thousands of years, and during that time a lot of shit went down. Plans were laid and either didn't pan out or were thwarted. Sleeper agents were never activated. Resources were depleted. And both sides have had a lot of time to think of a thousand different ways they could finally win the war. Importantly, I'm fairly sure they all have multiple fires in the oven at any given time. They're searching for a hundred different superweapons, studying a thousand different ways to restore their planet, etc.  What I'm getting at is, I don't think Megatron had literally planned on these exact events taking place. Rather, I think he's just making use of these resources as they are becoming available to him. So like, when he loses he takes a bit to figure out a course of action based on the circumstances at the time- which probably involves a lot of him going 'oh okay, so x thing happened 500 years ago, so if I combine that with y new thing that just happened I might be able to do z plan'. So in this way when some plan fails, he moves on to another one.  For instance, I imagine that the Decepticons knew about Earth all along- what with the Fallen being involved. So when Sentinel conspires with Megatron to betray the Autobots and rebuild Cybertron, and they suddenly have need of a slave-race, they have the perfect target in mind. When Sentinel crash lands, the Decepticons make a note of it, and plant the pillars around the globe just in case they can figure out a way to use the Space Bridge.  Also, I imagine this all happened like, hundreds of years ago when Cybertron was 'still alive' and they had access to the kind of resources needed to make mass interstellar travel a reality. Sort of like how if the US devolved in some sort of massive civil war, the government could probably launch a mission to the Moon if they thought it was necessary. But after a few decades of fighting, you'd be lucky to get up a single satellite.  I also imagine that doing all this requires a lot of energy, and one of the big things about the last movie was explaining how they can't make more Energon. I imagine all or most of their technology relies on that stuff for power. So I'm thinking the moon army was probably on Earth to oversee the search for the Allspark and Matrix, plus secure the Ark and pillars. As time went on and their energy problems worsened, they gradually mothballed these ships until there were none left active, and they had to use the pillars to bring them to Earth due to said lack of energy. As for why they were buried, well, presumably it was to camouflage them.  Or maybe it was just more convenient to space bridge them since they had it available. Space is awful big after all, flying at non relativistic speeds the trip from the Moon to Earth is between several hours and days.  Anyway, sometime after Sentinel crashlands the Decepticons discover the Allspark is on Earth. Now at this point, I imagine all the fighting-capable bots have been recalled to Cybertron or sent on more urgent missions, leaving only a handful of seekers who are all decrepit at this point and living on low-power mode, so they send out a signal instead of scouring the globe and securing it themselves. Megatron, wanting to ensure that no one gets any bright ideas, and also just out of sheer arrogance, goes for the Allspark personally, and crashlands in Antarctica.  In this way, going after the Allspark is just an opportunistic thing, not really a grand plan he's hinging everything on. Freezing in Antarctica is a massive setback, and all the Decepticons except some of the seekers have all left Earth at this point  Anyway, so after the events of Transformers, the Allspark is destroyed. And it was really the most convenient way of making Energon, but they do have another way- the harvester. It just requires Megatron to kill Optimus first because The Fallen ain't risking his million year-old ass on this. Obviously, it's better to have this portable cube with limitless energy which also acts as a reliquary of hidden knowledge, as opposed to this huge machine that destroys suns that you probably don't have the resources to move, requires you to find a seemingly unfindable artifact that you've been searching for for thousands of years and only two bots alive can use anyway, and to top it all off you have to kill the seemingly invincible murder machine that is Bayverse Optimus Prime- and we know Megatron would have done it already if he could. It's only due to the power boost of the allspark, ambushing him alone, the gang-up, and protecting Sam that Megatron was able to kill Optimus. I doubt he expected it to happen that quickly actually.  So yeah, Revenge of the Fallen was essentially Megatron going to plan B and getting lucky. Probably not something he was counting on, just something he took advantage of.  Finally we get to Dark of the Moon. At this point, Megatron is looking through his options and figures out that if he can trick Optimus into reviving Sentinel, the former Prime can take Optimus out in a surprise attack, they can activate the space bridge, and Sentinel will get the Matrix besides- might even be able to revive the Fallen with it.  So when you think of it like that, it makes sense. Megatron has been doing this for thousands of years, and as the war has gone on, both leaders have gotten fairly resourceful, but at the same time he's given up on any kind of traditional military victory and is grasping at straws.
How you feel about this movie, I feel about Revenge of the Fallen. Like, I know it's bad, but I unironically enjoy it.

Ah yes, the age old concept of applying Monday morning quarterback morality to the actions of a being who has had the biggest hand in saving the Earth and the whole of humanity THREE TIMES by this point. From the same faction of enemies no less. And he's somehow a bad guy for finally trying to ensure it doesn't happen a fourth time? Right. Despite how silly the movies can be, this is not Saturday morning cartoon Optimus, as much as I love that version. He really tried to not be as cutthroat in the first one. He was willing to sacrifice himself right from the very beginning instead of Megatron. I guess Sam is a war criminal too for using the cube on Megatron. But oh those poor Decepticons at the beginning of the second one just minding their own business. The ones who run and cause more collateral damage the second their cover is blown? The one who went on an immediate rampage down a busy freeway killing god knows how many people? The one who Optimus told to "stop and pull over" BEFORE shooting him down because he's still pancaking cars? The one who so innocently already knows about the Fallen's plans? Ok. Sure. Let him live. What could go wrong? The militaries of the world would absolutely be hunting down Decepticons after the events of the first film. If the Autobots had not been helping the military hunt them down people would be like "why aren't they helping them so maybe more soldiers don't die needlessly?" Don't forget....the Autobots are granted asylum....the Decepticons were not. They're on Earth against humany's will. There's a word for that. Hostile. So they kill at the drop of a hat and are actively still planning something and they all seem to be in on it. Oh wait....there's the part where Optimus rips that one's face apart in the forest. How horrible of him. It wasn't like he was being attacked three on one or anything. Or that he was trying to protect a person from being killed. A person they were actually after at that very moment. He even took the fight to a deserted place to minimize collateral damage. Which he does or tries to do every single time he has any control over where the fight happens. What a monster. To fight three by himself and die to save a kid. Did I see footage of what he did in Egypt to Megatron and the Fallen in there as examples of him being "too violent?" That was two on one again. He only wounded Megatron even though Megatron KILLED him earlier. And he shouldn't have killed the Fallen before the police arrived with their Decepticon sized handcuffs to arrest him. It wasn't like they were about to activate a device that would destroy the sun and Earth and everything. He should be nice and non-violent to them in the three minutes he has before they destroy the solar system. Now we're to Dark of the Moon. Humans are still giving the Autobots shit like they don't know what they're talking about. They've already caught Shockwave up to something sus as fu. They know Megatron and Starscream are still alive. How many Decepticons does Optimus kill in Dark of the Moon before they inflict a thousand 9/11s worth of damage to Chicago? Zero that I can recall. The first one being a Decepticon who was actively trying to kill people at that very moment. By this point, he's realized that their war is causing Earth way too much destruction constantly and the kid gloves aren't getting anything done. So he finally (justifiably) says "we're going to kill them all." Not killing them all hasn't been working so far. They keep coming back with ever more destructive plots that kill more people every time. It's almost like it's a last resort or something. Ya know, like even reasonable people can be pushed to if they finally reach their limit. They're about to enslave all the humans. The ones who survive anyway. Prime should just talk to them! It's not like this is the third and worst time they've done this or anything. Oh wait...he does try to talk to Sentinel. Who tells Optimus he'll kill him if he tries to stop him. The human casualties of the three films so far are astronomical. So obviously he should leave Megatron and Sentinel alive to be arrested. Because that's something that is possible. Yes, I know some Decepticons WERE incarcerated in The Last Knight. But A: Those were some real nobodies. Not Decepticons on the level of even Barricade or Starscream. B: That scene was played as a joke just to homage Con Air or Armageddon or something. And C: The Last Knight sucks and doesn't count lol. Anyways....if ("if" lol) it happens a fourth time because Optimus didn't end it when he has the chance, isn't that worse? What should he do? Take them and imprison them on Cybertron? Oh wait, he let Cybertron, his home, be destroyed to protect a perpetually ungrateful world. After alllll this, he would've looked like a chump for letting either Megatron or Sentinel live. Guaranteed they would try something again. Or, even worse, with Cybertron gone they just go full General Zod and decide to just kill everyone and everything completely because they have nothing left. So Optimus is a war criminal for finally having had enough and attempting to actually prevent anything like Chicago from ever happening again. Because a several million year old robot should defer to human laws when dealing with his own kind. That makes so much sense. People obviously know better than he does when it comes to dealing with Cybertronians. This is the stupidest argument. It's worse than the "should Batman just kill the Joker?" debate. The Joker can actually be incarcerated and won't live practically forever. And he plays a lot of murderous games. Megatron isn't playing games. His survival means genocide at the very least or even the actual apocalypse. And even then, he wasn't viciously outright killed by Prime until his third attempt. If this were real life (I know, I know) people would be dancing in the streets that Megatron and Sentinel were dead lol. The other (better) ending to Dark of the Moon works because Megatron shows his willingness to allow Optimus to kill him in a way that seems finally not like a trick. But the ending as is? Megatron is full of shit when he offers that truce. The fact that Optimus beheads him like that with one arm shows how much he must've been pulling his punches in the previous two. Especially the first one. Plus they both go through a few changes lulz. G1 Optimus is wonderful and I love him. But in a movie that's supposed to show a more "realistically" compassionate but battle hardened Prime, he cannot just keep forgiving and not ending this because the cartoon series doesn't have a harrowing body count for the Decepticons to answer for. And he would look like a completely ineffectual fool if he keeps choosing to not decisively do something about it. Originally, Micheal Bay wanted the movie to end with Optimus Prime and Megatron ending their war, and agreeing to join forces to allow Cybertron to be rebuilt. But, there were two factors that stopped this plan:  1. The Novel: The Novelization was released pre-maturely, and thus *spoiled* the ending of the movie! Because of this, not only was the ending changed to compensate, but no other novelizations of the remaining movies (AOE and TLK) were ever made!  2. Executives: If what happened in DOTM didnâ€™t say enough, Micheal Bay was *done* with the Transformers movies after three in a row, and wanted to move on. But, along with the Novel Incident, Paramount *demanded* that more movies would be made. As a result both AOE and TLK seemed to have a sense of hatred in it, as Optimus was kinda out of character, and how the humans werenâ€™t so forgiving.  Thatâ€™s basically what happened to the original ending! Thank you for reading!

Something I really disliked about these films was the characterization of Optimus Prime. Prime was someone who would show the enemy mercy first, and then fight later if it's the only way that's necessary. In the Bay films, he rarely shows mercy, and even taunts the enemy he's willingly trying to kill. Despite the spectacle being very fun to see, I hope the newer films will make Prime more of an inspiring and compassionate leader that can make mistakes but learn from them. Obviously yeah, the Decepticons are the enemy and as a soldier Prime needs to obviously extinguish the threat when necessary, but it has to have weight to it. Maybe Prime can hesitate sometimes, trying to show mercy until eventually choosing violence in an act of self defense or as a way to end the conflict. The Decepticons were supposed to be the brutal and merciless ones, contrasting with the heroic Autobots. I hope they don't get it twisted again. If they're ever gonna have a scene of a character killing waves and waves of nameless ones, then they should give the role to Megatron, who deserves to be feared by the audience.  Then again, this is probably just my own view of the character. I'm not the writer of these movies, or any transformers media. Just my worthless opinion, I guess.

The Russia-US Intelligence Black Hole actually makes plentiful sense.  We still know very little, save what we've garnered from refugees that fled the Soviet Union and *cough cough* National Socialist Wehrmacht Commanders post-WWII in exchange for asylum *cough*.  We really don't know, to what extent, the Soviets were typically up to. Hence why the Cold War was a game of Intelligence and Black Operations. CIA with their assets against the KGB and their assets.  Thus, yeah, it would be one of those "Shit, we don't know how they got it... We just found out ourselves that they had it when they contacted us to do a hand off with you guys and our operators,"  I mean this is the same intelligence cadre and US Intel Community that took 10 years to find one man responsible for 9/11. After invading two countries, tasking every branch, and every allied nation's intelligence communities, 13 DoD satellites (probably more), a network of spies and informants, and we only found him because two dudes in Pakistan said "Hey, we found this guy that matches the description, person, character, and mannerisms of Osama Bin Laden... And he lives in this compound and rarely leaves it. Oh, and he has like two or three personal couriers that frequently visit the place... Probs check it out CIA,"  What I appreciate is that the average American civilian tends to think that the US Intelligence and Counter-Intelligence communities are like these deeply big brain, super smart, capable, James Bond level super spies and analysts...  When really its just a typical echo-chamber of what we know, and what we assume we know based on what we know... Military Intelligence itself, is an "oxymoron". They use a lot of words that are synonymous to "we assume" or "its probable". When they start throwing that out there, its probably 95% shit with a nugget of gold at its center that you have to wipe the shit away to get to. And that gold is literally "The enemy is on the objective's location, expect contact, and expect it to be harder than it needs to be,"  The US Intelligence Community is hyped up, but the opposite is the reality. Most of the Branches have E3's and E4's running most intel analysis. The CIA only takes what's crucially necessary to address as legitimate threats to national security. But they all run around making assumptions because time frame necessitates action, because investigating probable cause, motive and means would take too long and would be far too late when they find that this X problem MUST be stopped.  This doesn't mean they're stupid. They're our best and brightest. Call me a Bay apologist, but I love Bayverse Transformers (at least the "original trilogy", as I call it). Transformers should NOT be some goofy blocky robots with cheesy lines (cough, G1, cough) - they are freakin giant aliens made of living metal, they are, just by description, supposed to be war machines! Exactly the ones that Bayverse movies show us! With alien designs and their own language (which Decepticons prefer to speak, whereas Autobots adapted to speak English to be understood by humans)! Living robots, who have been at war for eons, which resulted in their home planet literally unable to sustain life, arriving to Earth and bringing their war here! The concept itself, by definition, should be dark and adult - and that is exactly what DOTM is, what all Bayverse movies strived to be!

Here's my take.  I never watched the cartoon series or movies as a kid, nor have I as an adult.  I was 17 when the first Bayformers movie came out, and I thought it was pretty darn cool, but a little short on the giant robot fighting action for my taste.  I'll sacrifice dumb plot for the sake of cool action.  The second one came out, and I thought that was pretty cool too.  Obviously not taking itself too seriously, the plot is already nonsense, but I enjoyed it.  It's dumb, the characters are dumb, the plot is dumb, but my movie ticket doesn't say "Casablanca" or "The Return of the King" or some other well written movie on it.  I came to see robots fighting each other in a city.  My only disappointment was that the city was lame, dusty sand buildings.  Then the third one came out.  The conspiracy stuff was (dumb) fun.  The Sam stuff was... pretty boring, I could do without that, he really didn't need to be there.  But then.   The brutally violent alien invasion of a city with absolutely no hesitation about showing rampant death and destruction on a large scale is something I haven't seen done this well in any other movie besides Battle: Los Angeles.  Between the two, both have their ups and downs.  But the second half of this movie... it's just awesome.

About Megatron's plan: It could be possible that Megatron simply didn't know Sentinel was on the moon until after Revenge of the Fallen when he met up with Soundwave. I say this for a few reasons; Megatron's plan, as he stated himself, was to "rendez-vous here on this planet, before fate waylaid us both." The plan was to simply meet up on Earth, possibly because that's where the Allspark was. His ORIGINAL (keyword) plan never involved reviving (even though it wasn't revival because he never died, he was just in sleep mode) Sentinel and then doing all that. So now you ask; Why did the plan change?  Well, it was because, as Megatron put it, "Fate waylaid us both." It just so happened that they both crash landed, Megatron for unknown reasons (I personally wouldn't count S7's explanation as they themselves admit it's a theory) and Sentinel because he was shot down. Why was Sentinel shot down, despite Megatron's plan was for them to meet up? Because it was a secret from the entire deception army, barring the two waves (might be one or two more, but generally I'll just say them to be on the safe side.) My evidence for this was that even Starscream never knew about this, despite being in command of the deceptions TWICE and being Megatron's top underling. Megatron kept the plan a secre for unknown, but not unreasonable nor unrealistic, reasons.   So I covered why the plan changed, now I'll cover why and when the new plan started when it did. The TLDR answer: He simply didn't know the circumstances until after Revenge of the Fallen. My evidence for this is this: In the first movie Megatron simply wanted to retrieve the Allspark so he could rebuild Cybertron, and THEN he could meet up with Sentinel. The reason he didn't meet up with Sentinel prior to retrieving the Allspark could be for a few reasons: He was narrow sighted and laser focused purely on retrieving the Allspark, temporarily forgetting Sentinel because Sentinel isn't a top priority. Getting the Allspark before the autobots hide it in a much more secure location (whatever that might be) and risk loosing it forever. Another reason is that he thought he could just betray Sentinel once he gets the Allspark. No explanation given because it's just a Megatron thing to do. And the last reason, and personally what i believe is most realistic, is that he simply *didn't know* Sentinel crash landed on the moon. Sentinel crashed AFTER Megatron crashed on the North Pole. So there's no way for him to meet up with someone he doesn't know the situation, nor the location to. Remember that in the first movie Megatron was awake for 4 hours at BEST. So how could he have known the up to date situation about Sentinel when his main goal is to retrieve the Allspark, and 4 hours later he's offlined? In the second movie, same deal. He's awake for a week or so (at best) and his goal is to retrieve the Matrix of Leadership so they could activate the Star Harvester and make more energon, which was revealed to him after his resurrection by his master. That's why I say he knew after ROTF. Because that's the only time he could have know the situation.  So essentially: Megatron never knew about the army on the moon nor about Sentinel, since both arrived after Megatron's crashing on the NP. So while Megatron was in ice, the Decepticons under the command of Soundwave (i say him because he knew about the plans 100% and worked on them while Megatron was gone. My proof is the human villain saying that Soundwave is directly responsible for the Apollo program being cancelled, which means he was directly involved) would've raided the Ark for the pillars and then hid both themselves and the pillars underneath the moon's surface. They'd stay there in a statis mode (sorta like sentinel was) while the big named Decepticons from TF2007 locate Megatron and the cube. Two and a half movies later, Soundwave meets up with Megatron and fills him in on the situation (since this would be the first time they had the chance to) and Megatron would proceed with what options he had left. He would have the cons manipulate the bots into discovering and reviving sentinel (learning from the second movie that the matrix can repower bots) because Sentinel was the only bot who could control the pillars. Then they'd use the pillars for a SURPRISE attack (the Decepticons didn't require the pillars to travel to Earth like the guy said, since they got to the moon perfectly fine. It's just that the pillars was the fastest, and they needed to blitzkrieg the U.S. and the world to be able to get a stronghold quickly. Which would've worked has the autobots not returned) on the U.S. From there they'd transport Cybertron to Earth and use the humans for slave labor. But they failed, so it never happened.   And if you're saying that's impossible because it was never shown in the movie, remember this: Just because it wasn't shown doesn't mean it's impossible. We, the viewer, get shown the story through biased filters. We view it though, primarily, the eyes of Sam. Because of that we get cons who seem unemotional and uncharacterized, but that's only because that's how Sam sees them. Which is why they seem like cartoon villains at times who's evil just to be evil BECAUSE we see them through the eyes of Sam, one of their victims. I often find people ignore the fact that our viewpoint is biased when reviewing the plot of the first three. When if you take the viewpoint into account, the plot holes make sense as to why they exist.   But that's my Â¢2 on the matter  Edit: Typos

I will say I think the Mikaela situation was a pretty bad symptom of these movies over-relying on a human cast. Recasting a VA for a robot man is a lot easier than having to recast an actual actor, they're overlaid with so many filters minor differences would be pretty hard to spot and if it was different you could just pull a Bumblebee and say they got kick in the voicebox or something. Then by doing that you no longer run the risk of having to last-second write out an important character due to an acting dispute and replacing them with an obviously different person and ruining a story arc built up over 3 whole movies.

I am also going to point out that a YouTuber by the pseudonym Phoenix Studios is rewriting Michael Bay's _Transformers_ movies and those rewrites are surprisingly great!
